## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical reaction kinetics. Rate laws typically express dA/dt as polynomial, power-law, or rational functions of A.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of single species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed first+second order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel reaction pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with one species)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis, A catalyzes its own production)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme kinetics with inhibition at high concentration)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying external driving, e.g., photolysis with varying intensity)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional-order kinetics with background source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding or reaction)
- Second-order with depletion partner: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - c2 * A) (second-order reaction where B is stoichiometrically linked to A)
- Damped rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (concentration-dependent activation energy effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power law: if dA/dt depends on A^n, the exponent n indicates the reaction order, which reflects the molecularity of the rate-determining step
- Negative coefficients on A terms: a negative leading coefficient indicates consumption of species A (reactant disappearing)
- Rational functions of A: saturation in rate with increasing A suggests enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanisms with finite active sites
- Product of A and (constant - A): logistic-like terms indicate autocatalytic or competitive mechanisms where both reactant and product concentrations matter
- Explicit time dependence: if t appears directly in the rate law, it suggests an externally modulated process (e.g., varying temperature, light intensity) rather than a simple mass-action mechanism
- Sum of power-law terms in A: multiple additive terms suggest parallel reaction pathways each with distinct molecularity
- Exponential dependence on A: suggests concentration-dependent changes in mechanism or effective activation energy (non-Arrhenius behavior in concentration space)
- Constant additive term independent of A: indicates a zero-order source or sink (e.g., constant feed into reactor, photochemical generation)
